    19→  4. Password is wrong → `recordFailure()` is called  
    20→  5. `recordFailure` creates a NEW entry with count=1, resetAt=now+60s ← **this is correct**  
    21→  
    22→  But consider this alternate sequence where the caller calls recordFailure without checkRateLimit first (not currently happening in the codebase, but the API contract is fragile):  
    23→  1. 4 failures (count=4, resetAt=T+60s)  
    24→  2. Window expires  
    25→  3. `recordFailure()` called directly → entry still exists with count=4, `entry.resetAt` is in the past

    10→### [CC-001] `loadTeams()` migration calls `saveTeams()` without holding a lock — concurrent data race  
    11→- **File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/team-registry.ts`:206-215  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** race-condition  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `loadTeams()` is a public, non-async function called from many places (API GET routes, within `withLock` callbacks, etc.). When the one-time migration detects a team without a `type` field (line 208), it calls `saveTeams(teams)` on line 214. However, `loadTeams()` does not acquire any lock. If two concurrent requests both call `loadTeams()` and both trigger the migration, they will race on `writeFileSync`. More critically, `loadTeams()` is called *inside* `withLock('teams', ...)` callbacks (e.g., `createTeam` line 247, `updateTeam` line 279). If the migration fires inside that callback, it calls `saveTeams()` which is fine because it's already under the lock. But if the migration fires from an *unlocked* call (e.g., `getTeam()` on line 237, or any API GET handler), it writes to disk without synchronization, potentially clobbering a concurrent locked write.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→```typescript  
    18→// line 237 — getTeam reads without lock, can trigger migration write  
    19→export function getTeam(id: string): Team | null {  
    20→  const teams = loadTeams()  // <-- migration may call saveTeams() here, no lock  
    21→  return teams.find(t => t.id === id) || null  
    22→}  
    23→```  
    24→- **Fix:** Move the migration to a dedicated `migrateTeamsFile()` function called once at startup (e.g., in `server.mjs`), or wrap the migration save in `withLock('teams', ...)`. Al  

... [16032 more chars truncated]

    19→- **Description:** `requestTransfer` sends `requestedBy: agentId` (line 253) and `resolveTransfer` sends `resolvedBy: agentId` (line 272). Both callbacks correctly list `agentId` in their dependency arrays (lines 263, 282), so the closure will be recreated when `agentId` changes. However, the `agentId` parameter to `useGovernance` is typed `string | null`. If `agentId` is `null` at call time, the payloads send `requestedBy: null` / `resolvedBy: null` to the server. There is no guard like the one in `useTeam.updateTeam` (`if (!teamId) return`). If the server does not validate these fields, a transfer request could be created with `requestedBy: null`.  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→  ```typescript  
    22→  // line 253 — agentId may be null  
    23→  body: JSON.stringify({ agentId: targetAgentId, fromTeamId, toTeamId, requestedBy: agentId, note }),  
    24→  // line 272 — agentId may be null  
    25→  body: JSON.stringify({ action, resolvedBy: agentId, rejectReason }),  
    26→  ```  
    27→- **Fix:** Add an early-return guard at the top of both callbacks: `if (!agentId) return { success: false, error: 'No agent selected' }`. This matches the defensive pattern used in `useTeam.updateTeam` (line 44).  
    28→  
    29→### [CC-002] `refresh()` calls in mutation callbacks do not use AbortController, risking state updates after unmount  
    30→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useGovernance.  

... [8737 more chars truncated]  

</details>

    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** logic  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** The Escape key useEffect depends on `[isOpen]` but calls `handleClose`, which is defined inline and captures the `submitting` state. Because `handleClose` is not in the dependency array, pressing Escape during a submission will close the dialog even though `handleClose` checks `if (submitting) return` -- it reads a stale `submitting = false` closure. Additionally, React's exhaustive-deps lint rule would flag this.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```tsx  
    18→  useEffect(() => {  
    19→    if (!isOpen) return  
    20→    const handleKey = (e: KeyboardEvent) => { if (e.key === 'Escape') handleClose() }  
    21→    document.addEventListener('keydown', handleKey)  
    22→    return () => document.removeEventListener('keydown', handleKey)  
    23→  }, [isOpen])  // missing handleClose in deps  
    24→  ```  
    25→- **Fix:** Either wrap `handleClose` in `useCallback` and add it to the dependency array, or inline the submitting guard in the effect and add `submitting` to deps. Example: `}, [isOpen, submitting])` with an inline check.

    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/tests/transfer-registry.test.ts:11-21  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** api-contract  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `transfer-registry.ts` uses named imports (`import { readFileSync, writeFileSync, mkdirSync, existsSync } from 'fs'`), but the test mocks `fs` with top-level named exports (no `default` wrapper). Meanwhile, other test files (governance, team-registry, team-api, document-api, task-registry) mock `fs` with a `default:` wrapper because their corresponding implementation files use `import fs from 'fs'` (default import). The transfer-registry test is correct for its implementation -- this is NOT a bug. However, the inconsistency between test files is confusing and if someone refactors transfer-registry.ts to use `import fs from 'fs'` the test would silently break.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // transfer-registry.ts uses NAMED imports:  
    19→  import { readFileSync, writeFileSync, mkdirSync, existsSync } from 'fs'

    22→  vi.mock('fs', () => ({  
    23→    existsSync: vi.fn(...),  
    24→    readFileSync: vi.fn(...),  
    25→    writeFileSync: vi.fn(...),  
    26→    mkdirSync: vi.fn(),  
    27→  }))  
    28→  ```  
    29→- **Fix:** This is actually correctly matched to the implementation. Re-classifying to NIT for the inconsistency documentation concern. See CC-012.

/**  
 * Governance Library - Password management, manager role, and team role checks  
 *  
 * Storage: ~/.aimaestro/governance.json  
 * Follows the same synchronous file I/O pattern as lib/team-registry.ts  
 */  

import fs from 'fs'  
import path from 'path'  
import os from 'os'  
import bcrypt from 'bcryptjs'  
import { loadTeams, getTeam } from './team-registry'  
import { withLock } from '@/lib/file-lock'  
import type { GovernanceConfig } from '@/types/governance'  
import { DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG } from '@/types/governance'  
import type { Team } from '@/types/team'  

const AIMAESTRO_DIR = path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro')  
const GOVERNANCE_FILE = path.join(AIMAESTRO_DIR, 'governance.json')  

const BCRYPT_SALT_ROUNDS = 12  

/** Ensure ~/.aimaestro directory exists */  
function ensureAimaestroDir() {  
  if (!fs.existsSync(AIMAESTRO_DIR)) {  
    fs.mkdirSync(AIMAESTRO_DIR, { recursive: true })  
  }  
}  

/** Load governance config from disk, creating with defaults if missing */  
export function loadGovernance(): GovernanceConfig {  
  ensureAimaestroDir()  
  if (!fs.existsSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE)) {  
    // First-time initialization: write defaults and return them  
    saveGovernance(DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG)  
    return { ...DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG }  
  }  
  try {  
    const data = fs.readFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    const parsed: GovernanceConfig = JSON.parse(data)  
    return parsed  
  } catch (error) {  
    // Distinguish read errors from parse errors — parse errors indicate disk corruption  
    if (error instanceof SyntaxError) {  
      console.error('[governance] CORRUPTION: governance.json contains invalid JSON — returning defaults. Manual inspection required:', GOVERNANCE_FILE)  
    } else {  
      console.error('[governance] Failed to read governance config:', error)  
    }  
    return { ...DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG }  
  }  
}

 * Team Registry - File-based CRUD for team persistence

 * Storage: ~/.aimaestro/teams/teams.json

// --- Team Name Validation Constants ---  
// Mirrors agent name rigor from app/api/v1/register/route.ts but allows spaces/display chars  
const TEAM_NAME_MIN_LENGTH = 4  
const TEAM_NAME_MAX_LENGTH = 64  

/** Error thrown when team validation fails — caught by API routes to return proper HTTP status */  
export class TeamValidationException extends Error {  
  code: number  
  constructor(message: string, code: number) {  
    super(message)  
    this.name = 'TeamValidationException'  
    this.code = code  
  }  
}  

/**  
 * Sanitize a team name: strip control chars, collapse whitespace, trim.  
 * Same sanitization approach used by AI Maestro agent name validation  
 * but adapted for display names (allows spaces, mixed case).  
 */  
export function sanitizeTeamName(raw: string): string {  
  return raw  
    .replace(/[\x00-\x1F\x7F]/g, '')  // Strip control characters (same as agent name sanitization)  
    .replace(/\s+/g, ' ')              // Collapse all whitespace into single space  
    .trim()  
}

/**  
 * Transfer Registry — manages team transfer requests  
 *  
 * When a COS or MANAGER tries to move an agent from a closed team  
 * led by a different COS, a transfer request is created that must  
 * be approved by the source team's COS before the move takes effect.  
 */  

import { readFileSync, writeFileSync, mkdirSync, existsSync } from 'fs'  
import os from 'os'  
import path from 'path'  
import { randomUUID } from 'crypto'  
import type { TransferRequest, TransfersFile } from '@/types/governance'  
import { withLock } from '@/lib/file-lock'  

const AIMAESTRO_DIR = path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro')  
const TRANSFERS_FILE = path.join(AIMAESTRO_DIR, 'governance-transfers.json')  

function ensureDir(): void {  
  if (!existsSync(AIMAESTRO_DIR)) {  
    mkdirSync(AIMAESTRO_DIR, { recursive: true })  
  }  
}  

/** Load all transfer requests from disk */  
export function loadTransfers(): TransferRequest[] {  
  ensureDir()  
  if (!existsSync(TRANSFERS_FILE)) {  
    return []  
  }  
  try {  
    const raw = readFileSync(TRANSFERS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    const data: TransfersFile = JSON.parse(raw)  
    return data.requests || []  
  } catch {  
    return []  
  }  
}  

/** Save transfer requests to disk */  
function saveTransfers(requests: TransferRequest[]): void {  
  ensureDir()  
  const data: TransfersFile = { version: 1, requests }  
  writeFileSync(TRANSFERS_FILE, JSON.stringify(data, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
}

      createdAt: new Date().toISOString(),

/**  
 * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
 *  
 * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
 * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
 * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
 * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
 */  

import { loadGovernance } from './governance'  
import { loadTeams } from './team-registry'  

export interface MessageFilterInput {  
  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
  recipientAgentId: string  
}  

export interface MessageFilterResult {  
  allowed: boolean  
  reason?: string  
}  

/**  
 * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
 *  
 * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
 * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
 * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
 * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
 * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
 * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
 * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
 * 7. Default: allowed  
 *  
 * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
 * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
 */  
export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  

  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    return { allowed: true }  
  }  

  // Single snapshot of all state — avoids redundant file reads from governance helpers  
  const teams = loadTeams()  
  const governance = loadGovernance()  

  // Derive closed-team membership from the single snapshot  
  const closedTeams = teams.filter(t => t.type === 'closed')  
  const senderTeams = closedTeams.filter(t => t.agentIds.includes(senderAgentId))  
  c

/**  
 * Task Registry - File-based CRUD for team task persistence  
 *  
 * Storage: ~/.aimaestro/teams/tasks-{teamId}.json (one per team)  
 * Mirrors the pattern from lib/team-registry.ts  
 */  

import fs from 'fs'  
import path from 'path'  
import os from 'os'  
import { v4 as uuidv4 } from 'uuid'  
import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
import { withLock } from '@/lib/file-lock'  
import type { Task, TaskWithDeps, TasksFile } from '@/types/task'  

const TEAMS_DIR = path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro', 'teams')  

function ensureTeamsDir() {  
  if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_DIR)) {  
    fs.mkdirSync(TEAMS_DIR, { recursive: true })  
  }  
}  

function tasksFilePath(teamId: string): string {  
  // Validate teamId is a proper UUID to prevent path traversal attacks  
  // Strict UUID v4 pattern (8-4-4-4-12 hex groups) to prevent path traversal  
  if (!/^[0-9a-f]{8}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{12}$/i.test(teamId)) throw new Error('Invalid team ID')  
  // Defense-in-depth: use basename to strip any directory components  
  return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`tasks-${teamId}.json`))  
}  

export function loadTasks(teamId: string): Task[] {  
  try {  
    ensureTeamsDir()  
    const filePath = tasksFilePath(teamId)  
    if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) {  
      return []  
    }  
    const data = fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8')  
    const parsed: TasksFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    return Array.isArray(parsed.tasks) ? parsed.tasks : []  
  } catch (error) {  
    console.error(`Failed to load tasks for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    return []  
  }  
}  

export function saveTasks(teamId: string, tasks: Task[]): boolean {  
  try {  
    ensureTeamsDir()  
    const file: TasksFile = { version: 1, tasks }  
    fs.writeFileSync(tasksFilePath(teamId), JSON.stringify(file, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    return true  
  } catch (error) {  
    console.error(`Failed to save tasks for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    return false  
  }  
}  

/**  
 * Resolve task dependencies and compute derived fields  
 */  


... [4615 more chars truncated]

/**

    fs.mkdirSync(TEAMS_DIR, { recursive: true })  
  }  
}  

function docsFilePath(teamId: string): string {  
  return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, `docs-${teamId}.json`)  
}  

export function loadDocuments(teamId: string): TeamDocument[] {  
  try {  
    ensureTeamsDir()  
    const filePath = docsFilePath(teamId)  
    if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) {  
      return []  
    }  
    const data = fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8')  
    const parsed: TeamDocumentsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    return Array.isArray(parsed.documents) ? parsed.documents : []  
  } catch (error) {  
    console.error(`Failed to load documents for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    return []  
  }  
}  

export function saveDocuments(teamId: string, documents: TeamDocument[]): boolean {  
  try {  
    ensureTeamsDir()  
    const file: TeamDocumentsFile = { version: 1, documents }  
    fs.writeFileSync(docsFilePath(teamId), JSON.stringify(file, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    return true  
  } catch (error) {  
    console.error(`Failed to save documents for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    return false  
  }  
}  

export function getDocument(teamId: string, docId: string): TeamDocument | null {  
  const documents = loadDocuments(teamId)  
  return documents.find(d => d.id === docId) || null  
}  

export function createDocument(data: {  
  teamId: string  
  title: string  
  content: string  
  pinned?: boolean  
  tags?: string[]  
}): TeamDocument {  
  const documents = loadDocuments(data.teamId)  
  const now = new Date().toISOString()  

  const doc: TeamDocument =

import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
import { loadTeams, createTeam, TeamValidationException } from '@/lib/team-registry'  
import { getManagerId } from '@/lib/governance'  
import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  

// GET /api/teams - List all teams  
// Phase 1: localhost-only, no auth required. TODO: add ACL for Phase 2 remote access  
export async function GET() {  
  const teams = loadTeams()  
  return NextResponse.json({ teams })  
}  

// POST /api/teams - Create a new team  
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
  try {  
    const body = await request.json()  
    const { name, description, agentIds, type, chiefOfStaffId } = body  

    if (!name || typeof name !== 'string') {  
      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team name is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    }  

    if (agentIds && !Array.isArray(agentIds)) {  
      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentIds must be an array' }, { status: 400 })  
    }  

    // Pass managerId for multi-closed-team constraint checks (R4.1)  
    const managerId = getManagerId()  
    // Load agent names to prevent team/agent name collisions (R2.1)  
    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    const agentNames = allAgents.map(a => a.name).filter(Boolean) as string[]  
    const team = await createTeam({ name, description, agentIds: agentIds || [], type, chiefOfStaffId }, managerId, agentNames)  
    return NextResponse.json({ team }, { status: 201 })  
  } catch (error) {  
    // TeamValidationException carries the correct HTTP status code from business rule validation  
    if (error instanceof TeamValidationException) {  
      return NextResponse.json({ error: error.message }, { status: error.code })  
    }  
    console.error('Failed to create team:', error)  
    return NextResponse.json(  
      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to create team' },  
      { status: 500 }  
    )  
  }  
}

// POST /api/teams/[id]/documents - Create a new document  
export async function POST(  
  request: NextRequest,  
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
) {

    const { id } = await params  
    const team = getTeam(id)  
    if (!team) {  
      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })

import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
import { getDocument, updateDocument, deleteDocument } from '@/lib/document-registry'

// GET /api/teams/[id]/documents/[docId] - Get a single document  
export async function GET(  
  _request: NextRequest,  
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string; docId: string }> }  
) {  
  const { id, docId } = await params  
  const team = getTeam(id)  
  if (!team) {  
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })  
  }  
  const document = getDocument(id, docId)  
  if (!document) {  
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Document not found' }, { status: 404 })  
  }  
  return NextResponse.json({ document })  
}  

// PUT /api/teams/[id]/documents/[docId] - Update a document  
export async function PUT(  
  request: NextRequest,  
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string; docId: string }> }  
) {  
  try {  
    const { id, docId } = await params  
    const body = await request.json()  
    const updates: Record<string, unknown> = {}  
    if (body.title !== undefined) updates.title = body.title  
    if (body.content !== undefined) updates.content = body.content  
    if (body.pinned !== undefined) updates.pinned = body.pinned  
    if (body.tags !== undefined) updates.tags = body.tags  

    const document = updateDocument(id, docId, updates as any)  
    if (!document) {  
      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Document not found' }, { status: 404 })  
    }  

    return NextResponse.json({ document })  
  } catch (error) {  
    console.error('Failed to update document:', error)  
    return NextResponse.json(  
      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to update document' },  
      { status: 500 }  
    )  
  }  
}

/**  
 * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
 *  
 * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
 * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
 * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
 *  
 * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
 * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
 */  

// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
// Set of currently held lock names  
const held = new Set<string>()  

/**  
 * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
 * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
 */  
export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    held.add(name)  
    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
  }  

  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
      locks.set(name, [])  
    }  
    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    })  
  })  
}  

/**  
 * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
 */  
function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
  const queue = locks.get(name)  
  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    const next = queue.shift()!  
    if (queue.length === 0) {  
      locks.delete(name)  
    }  
    next()  
  } else {  
    // No waiters — release the lock  
    held.delete(name)  
    locks.delete(name)  
  }  
}  

/**  
 * Run a function under a named lock.  
 * Convenience wrapper: acquires, runs fn, releases (even on error).  
 */  
export async function withLock<T>(name: string, fn: () => T | Promise<T>): Promise<T> {  
  const release = await acquireLock(name)  
  try {  
    return await fn()  
  } finally {  
    rel  

... [12 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     2→import { loadGovernance, setPassword, verifyPassword } from '@/lib/governance'  
     3→import { checkRateLimit, recordFailure, resetRateLimit } from '@/lib/rate-limit'  
     4→  
     5→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
     6→  try {  
     7→    const body = await request.json()  
     8→    const { password, currentPassword } = body  
     9→  
    10→    if (!password || typeof password !== 'string' || password.length < 6) {  
    11→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Password must be at least 6 characters' }, { status: 400 })  
    12→    }  
    13→  
    14→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    15→  
    16→    // If password already set, require current password  
    17→    if (config.passwordHash) {  
    18→      // Rate limit password verification to prevent brute-force attacks  
    19→      const rateCheck = checkRateLimit('governance-password')  
    20→      if (!rateCheck.allowed) {  
    21→        return NextResponse.json(  
    22→          { error: `Too many failed password attempts. Try again in ${Math.ceil(rateCheck.retryAfterMs / 1000)}s` },  
    23→          { status: 429 }  
    24→        )  
    25→      }  
    26→  
    27→      if (!currentPassword || !(await verifyPassword(currentPassword))) {  
    28→        recordFailure('governance-password')  
    29→        return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid current password' }, { status: 401 })  
    30→      }  
    31→      // Password verified successfully — reset rate limit counter  
    32→      resetRateLimit('governance-password')  
    33→    }  
    34→  
    35→    const isChange = !!config.passwordHash  
    36→    await setPassword(password)  
    37→  
    38→    if (isChange) {  
    39→      console.log('[governance] Password changed at', new Date().toISOString())  
    40→    } else {  
    41→      console.log('[governance] Password set at', new Date().toISOString())  
    42→    }  
    43→  
    44→    return NextResponse.json({ success: true })

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    // Check cache first  
    19→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    20→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    25→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    26→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    27→  
    28→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    29→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    30→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    31→  
    32→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    33→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    34→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    35→      })  
    36→  
    37→      if (result.allowed) {  
    38→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    39→      }  
    40→    }  
    41→  
    42→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    43→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    44→  
    45→    // Evict stale/expired entries on every cache write to prevent unbounded growth  
    46→    const now = Date.now()  
    47→    for (const [key, entry] of cache) {  
    48→      if (now >= entry.expiresAt) cache.delete(key)  
    49→    }  
    50→  
    51→    r

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 17:28:23]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `rate-limit.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/rate-limit.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * Simple in-memory rate limiter for governance password operations.  
     3→ * Tracks failed attempts per key with a sliding time window.  
     4→ * Phase 1 only — no distributed state needed for localhost.  
     5→ */  
     6→  
     7→const limits = new Map<string, { count: number; resetAt: number }>()  
     8→  
     9→const DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS = 5  
    10→const DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS = 60_000 // 1 minute  
    11→  
    12→/** Check if the rate limit allows another attempt */  
    13→export function checkRateLimit(  
    14→  key: string,  
    15→  maxAttempts: number = DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS,  
    16→  windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS  
    17→): { allowed: boolean; retryAfterMs: number } {  
    18→  const now = Date.now()  
    19→  const entry = limits.get(key)  
    20→  
    21→  // Window expired — reset  
    22→  if (entry && now >= entry.resetAt) {  
    23→    limits.delete(key)  
    24→    return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    25→  }  
    26→  
    27→  // Check if over limit  
    28→  if (entry && entry.count >= maxAttempts) {  
    29→    return { allowed: false, retryAfterMs: entry.resetAt - now }  
    30→  }  
    31→  
    32→  return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    33→}  
    34→  
    35→/** Record a failed attempt */  
    36→export function recordFailure(key: string, windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS): void {  
    37→  const now = Date.now()  
    38→  const entry = limits.get(key) || { count: 0, resetAt: now + windowMs }  
    39→  limits.set(key, { count: entry.count + 1, resetAt: entry.resetAt })  
    40→}  
    41→  
    42→/** Reset rate limit on successful attempt */  
    43→export function resetRateLimit(key: string): void {  
    44→  limits.delete(key)  
    45→}  
    46→  
    47→// Periodic cleanup to prevent Map from growing unbounded  
    48→// (defensive — governance operations are infrequent so this rarely matters)

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts",
  "offset": 1,
  "limit": 100
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

    18→    }

    20→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    21→    if (!config.passwordHash) {  
    22→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Governance password not set' }, { status: 400 })

    27→    if (!rateCheck.allowed) {

    30→        { status: 429 }  
    31→      )  
    32→    }  
    33→  
    34→    // Password auth is stronger than ACL — only managers know the governance password  
    35→    if (!(await verifyPassword(password))) {  
    36→      recordFailure('governance-password')  
    37→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid governance password' }, { status: 401 })  
    38→    }  
    39→    // Password verified successfully — reset rate limit counter

    12→// Named HostTransferRequest to avoid collision with governance TransferRequest in transfer-registry.ts  
    13→interface HostTransferRequest {  
    14→  targetHostId: string  
    15→  targetHostUrl: string  
    16→  mode: 'move' | 'clone'  
    17→  newAlias?: string  
    18→  cloneRepositories?: boolean  
    19→}  
    20→  
    21→/**  
    22→ * POST /api/agents/[id]/transfer  
    23→ * Transfer an agent to another AI Maestro instance  
    24→ *  
    25→ * Body:  
    26→ * - targetHostId: ID of the target host  
    27→ * - targetHostUrl: URL of the target AI Maestro instance  
    28→ * - mode: 'move' (delete source) or 'clone' (keep source)  
    29→ * - newAlias: Optional new alias for the agent on target  
    30→ */  
    31→export async function POST(  
    32→  request: NextRequest,  
    33→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
    34→) {  
    35→  try {  
    36→    const { id } = await params  
    37→  
    38→    // Find agent by ID or alias  
    39→    let agent = getAgent(id)  
    40→    if (!agent) {  
    41→      agent = getAgentByAlias(id)

    43→  
    44→    if (!agent) {

    46→    }

     1→/**  
     2→ * AMP v1 Route Endpoint  
     3→ *  
     4→ * POST /api/v1/route  
     5→ *  
     6→ * Routes a message to the recipient agent within the local mesh network.  
     7→ * This is the primary message-sending endpoint for AMP providers.  
     8→ *  
     9→ * Authentication:  
    10→ *   - Bearer token (API key) for direct agent requests  
    11→ *   - X-Forwarded-From header for mesh-forwarded requests from known hosts  
    12→ *  
    13→ * Delivery methods:  
    14→ *   1. Local delivery — file system inbox + tmux notification (agent on this host)  
    15→ *   2. Mesh forwarding — HTTP POST to peer host's /api/v1/route (agent on another host)  
    16→ *   3. Relay queue — store-and-forward when recipient is offline or unreachable  
    17→ *  
    18→ * External providers (e.g. crabmail.ai) are rejected with 422 — clients must  
    19→ * send directly to the external provider using its route_url from registration.  
    20→ *  
    21→ * Resolution flow:  
    22→ *   1. Mesh-forwarded request? → local-only lookup (loop guard: never re-forward)  
    23→ *   2. Explicit remote host in address? → trust it, forward directly  
    24→ *   3. Otherwise? → checkMeshAgentExists (local first, then all peers)  
    25→ *   4. Resolved remote? → forwardToHost() → queue on failure  
    26→ *   5. Resolved local? → inbox write + tmux notification  
    27→ *   6. Not found anywhere? → inbox write + relay queue  
    28→ */

     1→/**  
     2→ * Simple in-memory rate limiter for governance password operations.  
     3→ * Tracks failed attempts per key with a sliding time window.  
     4→ * Phase 1 only — no distributed state needed for localhost.  
     5→ */  
     6→  
     7→const limits = new Map<string, { count: number; resetAt: number }>()  
     8→  
     9→const DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS = 5  
    10→const DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS = 60_000 // 1 minute  
    11→  
    12→/** Check if the rate limit allows another attempt */  
    13→export function checkRateLimit(  
    14→  key: string,  
    15→  maxAttempts: number = DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS,  
    16→  windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS  
    17→): { allowed: boolean; retryAfterMs: number } {  
    18→  const now = Date.now()  
    19→  const entry = limits.get(key)  
    20→  
    21→  // Window expired — reset  
    22→  if (entry && now >= entry.resetAt) {  
    23→    limits.delete(key)  
    24→    return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    25→  }  
    26→  
    27→  // Check if over limit  
    28→  if (entry && entry.count >= maxAttempts) {  
    29→    return { allowed: false, retryAfterMs: entry.resetAt - now }  
    30→  }  
    31→  
    32→  return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    33→}  
    34→  
    35→/** Record a failed attempt */  
    36→export function recordFailure(key: string, windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS): void {  
    37→  const now = Date.now()  
    38→  const entry = limits.get(key) || { count: 0, resetAt: now + windowMs }  
    39→  limits.set(key, { count: entry.count + 1, resetAt: entry.resetAt })  
    40→}  
    41→  
    42→/** Reset rate limit on successful attempt */  
    43→export function resetRateLimit(key: string): void {  
    44→  limits.delete(key)  
    45→}  
    46→  
    47→// Periodic cleanup to prevent Map from growing unbounded  
    48→// (defensive — governance operations are infrequent so this rarely matters)  
    49→if (typeof setInterval !== 'undefined') {  
    50→  setInterval(() => {  
    51→    const now = Date.now()  
    52→    for (const [key, entry] o

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.

    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }  
    45→  
    46→  // Single snapshot of all state — avoids redundant file reads from

    80→      return { allowed: true }  
    81→    }  
    82→    // COS-to-COS bridge: any COS can message any other COS  
    83→    if (agentIsCOS(recipientAgentId)) {  
    84→      return { allowed: true }

   103→    const shareTeam = senderTeams.some(team =>  
   104→      recipientTeams.some(rt => rt.id === team.id)  
   105→    )  
   106→    if (shareTeam) {  
   107→      return { allowed: true }  
   108→    }  
   109→    // Can message the COS of their own team  
   110→    const canReachCOS = senderTeams.some(team => team.chiefOfStaffId === recipientAgentId)  
   111→    if (canReachCOS) {  
   112→      return { allowed: true }  
   113→    }  
   114→    return {  
   115→      allowed: false,  
   116→      reason: 'Closed team members can only message within their team',  
   117→    }  
   118→  }  
   119→  
   120→  // Step 6: Sender is NOT in any closed team but recipient IS in a closed team (R6.5)  
   121→  if (!senderInClosed && recipientInClosed) {  
   122→    return {  
   123→      allowed: false,  
   124→      reason: 'Cannot message agents in closed teams from outside',  
   125→    }  
   126→  }  
   127→  
   128→  // Step 7: Default — allow  
   129→  return { allowed: true }  
   130→}

    18→function ensureTeamsDir() {

    23→  
    24→function tasksFilePath(teamId: string): string {  
    25→  // Validate teamId is a proper UUID to prevent path traversal attacks  
    26→  // Strict UUID v4 pattern (8-4-4-4-12 hex groups) to prevent path traversal  
    27→  if (!/^[0-9a-f]{8}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{12}$/i.test(teamId)) throw new Error('Invalid team ID')  
    28→  // Defense-in-depth: use basename to strip any directory components  
    29→  return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`tasks-${teamId}.json`))  
    30→}  
    31→  
    32→export function loadTasks(teamId: string): Task[] {  
    33→  try {  
    34→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    35→    const filePath = tasksFilePath(teamId)  
    36→    if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) {  
    37→      return []  
    38→    }  
    39→    const data = fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8')  
    40→    const parsed: TasksFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    41→    return Array.isArray(parsed.tasks) ? parsed.tasks : []  
    42→  } catch (error) {  
    43→    console.error(`Failed to load tasks for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    44→    return []  
    45→  }  
    46→}

     1→# PR: Team Governance Enforcement  
     2→  
     3→## Summary  
     4→  
     5→Implements team governance enforcement for AI Maestro's multi-agent messaging system:  
     6→  
     7→- **Team types**: `open` (unrestricted) and `closed` (messaging isolation, COS required)  
     8→- **Roles**: MANAGER (global singleton), Chief-of-Staff (per closed team), Normal  
     9→- **Message filtering**: 7-step `checkMessageAllowed()` blocks unauthorized cross-team messages for closed teams  
    10→- **Resource ACL**: `checkTeamAccess()` enforces read/write permissions based on role  
    11→- **Business rules**: `validateTeamMutation()` centralizes 8 rules (R1-R8) for team state transitions  
    12→- **Transfer system**: Agents request transfers between teams; MANAGER approves/rejects  
    13→- **File locking**: `withLock()` mutex prevents concurrent file corruption  
    14→- **UI**: Role badges, team membership panel, governance password dialog, transfer approval workflow

  4001→+}  
  4002→+  
  4003→+/**  
  4004→+ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
  4005→+ */  
  4006→+function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
  4007→+  const queue = locks.get(name)  
  4008→+  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
  4009→+    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
  4010→+    const next = queue.shift()!  
  4011→+    if (queue.length === 0) {  
  4012→+      locks.delete(name)  
  4013→+    }  
  4014→+    next()  
  4015→+  } else {  
  4016→+    // No waiters — release the lock  
  4017→+    held.delete(name)  
  4018→+    locks.delete(name)  
  4019→+  }  
  4020→+}  
  4021→+  
  4022→+/**  
  4023→+ * Run a function under a named lock.  
  4024→+ * Convenience wrapper: acquires, runs fn, releases (even on error).  
  4025→+ */  
  4026→+export async function withLock<T>(name: string, fn: () => T | Promise<T>): Promise<T> {  
  4027→+  const release = await acquireLock(name)  
  4028→+  try {  
  4029→+    return await fn()  
  4030→+  } finally {  
  4031→+    release()  
  4032→+  }  
  4033→+}

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→

    11→import { loadTeams } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    14→  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    15→  recipientAgentId: string  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     1→/**  
     2→ * Simple in-memory rate limiter for governance password operations.  
     3→ * Tracks failed attempts per key with a sliding time window.  
     4→ * Phase 1 only — no distributed state needed for localhost.  
     5→ */  
     6→  
     7→const limits = new Map<string, { count: number; resetAt: number }>()  
     8→  
     9→const DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS = 5  
    10→const DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS = 60_000 // 1 minute  
    11→  
    12→/** Check if the rate limit allows another attempt */  
    13→export function checkRateLimit(  
    14→  key: string,  
    15→  maxAttempts: number = DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS,  
    16→  windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS  
    17→): { allowed: boolean; retryAfterMs: number } {  
    18→  const now = Date.now()  
    19→  const entry = limits.get(key)  
    20→  
    21→  // Window expired — reset  
    22→  if (entry && now >= entry.resetAt) {  
    23→    limits.delete(key)  
    24→    return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    25→  }  
    26→  
    27→  // Check if over limit  
    28→  if (entry && entry.count >= maxAttempts) {  
    29→    return { allowed: false, retryAfterMs: entry.resetAt - now }  
    30→  }  
    31→  
    32→  return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    33→}  
    34→  
    35→/** Record a failed attempt */  
    36→export function recordFailure(key: string, windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS): void {  
    37→  const now = Date.now()  
    38→  const entry = limits.get(key) || { count: 0, resetAt: now + windowMs }  
    39→  limits.set(key, { count: entry.count + 1, resetAt: entry.resetAt })  
    40→}  
    41→  
    42→/** Reset rate limit on successful attempt */  
    43→export function resetRateLimit(key: string): void {  
    44→  limits.delete(key)  
    45→}  
    46→  
    47→// Periodic cleanup to prevent Map from growing unbounded  
    48→// (defensive — governance operations are infrequent so this rarely matters)  
    49→if (typeof setInterval !== 'undefined') {  
    50→  setInterval(() => {  
    51→    const now = Date.now()  
    52→    for (const [key, entry] o

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 17:28:55]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `rate-limit.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/rate-limit.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * Simple in-memory rate limiter for governance password operations.  
     3→ * Tracks failed attempts per key with a sliding time window.  
     4→ * Phase 1 only — no distributed state needed for localhost.  
     5→ */  
     6→  
     7→const limits = new Map<string, { count: number; resetAt: number }>()  
     8→  
     9→const DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS = 5  
    10→const DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS = 60_000 // 1 minute  
    11→  
    12→/** Check if the rate limit allows another attempt */  
    13→export function checkRateLimit(  
    14→  key: string,  
    15→  maxAttempts: number = DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS,  
    16→  windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS  
    17→): { allowed: boolean; retryAfterMs: number } {  
    18→  const now = Date.now()  
    19→  const entry = limits.get(key)  
    20→  
    21→  // Window expired — reset  
    22→  if (entry && now >= entry.resetAt) {  
    23→    limits.delete(key)  
    24→    return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    25→  }  
    26→  
    27→  // Check if over limit  
    28→  if (entry && entry.count >= maxAttempts) {  
    29→    return { allowed: false, retryAfterMs: entry.resetAt - now }  
    30→  }  
    31→

     1→/**  
     2→ * Simple in-memory rate limiter for governance password operations.  
     3→ * Tracks failed attempts per key with a sliding time window.  
     4→ * Phase 1 only — no distributed state needed for localhost.  
     5→ */  
     6→  
     7→const limits = new Map<string, { count: number; resetAt: number }>()  
     8→  
     9→const DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS = 5  
    10→const DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS = 60_000 // 1 minute  
    11→  
    12→/** Check if the rate limit allows another attempt */  
    13→export function checkRateLimit(  
    14→  key: string,  
    15→  maxAttempts: number = DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS,  
    16→  windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS  
    17→): { allowed: boolean; retryAfterMs: number } {  
    18→  const now = Date.now()  
    19→  const entry = limits.get(key)  
    20→  
    21→  // Window expired — reset  
    22→  if (entry && now >= entry.resetAt) {  
    23→    limits.delete(key)  
    24→    return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    25→  }  
    26→  
    27→  // Check if over limit  
    28→  if (entry && entry.count >= maxAttempts) {  
    29→    return { allowed: false, retryAfterMs: entry.resetAt - now }  
    30→  }  
    31→  
    32→  return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    33→}  
    34→  
    35→/** Record a failed attempt */  
    36→export function recordFailure(key: string, windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS): void {  
    37→  const now = Date.now()  
    38→  const entry = limits.get(key) || { count: 0, resetAt: now + windowMs }  
    39→  limits.set(key, { count: entry.count + 1, resetAt: entry.resetAt })  
    40→}  
    41→  
    42→/** Reset rate limit on successful attempt */  
    43→export function resetRateLimit(key: string): void {  
    44→  limits.delete(key)  
    45→}

    48→// (defensive — governance operations are infrequent so this rarely matters)

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 17:32:19]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 17:28:27]*

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 17:29:42]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have a thorough understanding. Let me also verify one more detail - whether the `resolveTransferRequest` call inside the teams lock acquires a second lock (the "transfers" lock), which could cause deadlock:  

Looking at the code: `resolveTransferRequest` uses `withLock('transfers', ...)` (line 98 of transfer-registry.ts), and the calling code holds `acquireLock('teams')` (line 42 of resolve route). These are different named locks, so no deadlock. However, the `revertTransferToPending` in the finally-adjacent catch on line 129 also acquires the 'transfers' lock. Let me verify there's no lock held at that point... The revert happens inside the `try` block but still under the 'teams' lock. That's fine since it's 'transfers' lock, not 'teams' lock.  

Now let me check one more detail - whether early returns inside the `try` block with `acquireLock` properly release:  

Looking at lines 42-135 of the resolve route: The `releaseLock()` is in `finally`, so all early returns (lines 52, 59, 70, 84-87, 97) will properly release the lock. Good.  

Now let me verify the `updateTask` timestamp logic more carefully. On line 157 of task-registry.ts, `tasks[index].startedAt` has already been overwritten by the spread on line 150-154. Let me trace this:  

Line 150-154: `tasks[index] = { ...tasks[index], ...updates, updatedAt: now }` -- this overwrites `startedAt` if it was in `updates`. Then line 157 checks `!tasks[index].startedAt`. But `updates` doesn't include `startedAt` (it's not in the `Partial<Pick<...>>` on line 139). So `startedAt` comes from the original `tasks[index]`, which is correct.  

Wait -- but `startedAt` is NOT in the Pick type on line 139 (`'subject' | 'description' | 'status' | 'assigneeAgentId' | 'blockedBy' | 'priority'`). So `updates` can never contain `startedAt`. That's fine, the spread won't overwrite it.  

Now let me check the `completedAt` timestamp logic on line 160: after line 150 spread, if `updates.status === 'completed'` and `tasks[index].completedAt` was already set from a previous completion... but wait, the task was changed via the spread at line 150 -- `tasks[index]` now has the new values including `status: 'completed'`. Line 160 checks `!tasks[index].completedAt` -- since `completedAt` is not in the `Pick`, it retains the original value. If the task was previously completed, had `completedAt` set, then moved back to `in_progress`, then moved to `completed` again, `completedAt` would still hold the old value. That's actually a bug -- re-completion doesn't update the timestamp.  

Let me now write the full report.  

</div>
